рҹҗі Container Services Integration
рҹ“Ұ Running Django Containers on EC2
# Option 1: Docker on EC2 (Simple)
# Install Docker on EC2 instance
sudo yum update -y
sudo yum install -y docker
sudo service docker start
sudo usermod -a -G docker ec2-user

# Build and run anihpj container
docker build -t anihpj:latest .
docker run -d -p 80:8000 \
    -e DATABASE_URL=postgresql://... \
    -e SECRET_KEY=... \
    --name anihpj-container \
    anihpj:latest

# Option 2: ECS (Elastic Container Service) on EC2
# More managed, integrates with ALB, Auto Scaling
aws ecs create-cluster --cluster-name anihpj-cluster

# Option 3: EKS (Elastic Kubernetes Service)
# For complex microservices architectures
# Overkill for single Django application
рҹ’Ө EC2 Hibernation
Hibernation saves RAM to EBS, faster boot than cold start.

в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
в”Ӯ  Standard Stop/Start:                              в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Stop вҶ’ 30-60 seconds вҶ’ Start                      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў OS boots from scratch                           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Applications restart                            в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Cache rebuilds                                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                                     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  With Hibernation:                                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Hibernate вҶ’ 5-10 seconds вҶ’ Resume                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў RAM restored from EBS                           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Applications resume instantly                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Cache preserved                                 в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                                     в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Use for anihpj:                                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Dev/staging environments (save costs)           в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Preserve application state                      в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  вҖў Faster startup for scheduled workloads          в”Ӯ
в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

# Enable hibernation
aws ec2 run-instances \
    --image-id ami-0c7217cdde317cfec \
    --instance-type m5.large \
    --hibernation-options Configured=true \
    --block-device-mappings '[
        {
            "DeviceName": "/dev/xvda",
            "Ebs": {
                "VolumeSize": 30,
                "Encrypted": true
            }
        }
    ]'
вҡҷпёҸ Nitro System
AWS Nitro System is the underlying platform for modern EC2 instances.

Benefits:
вң… Better performance (dedicated hardware for networking, storage)
вң… Enhanced security (hypervisor offloaded to dedicated hardware)
вң… More instance sizes and types
вң… Bare metal instances available
вң… Better price/performance

All modern instance types (M5, C5, R5, T3, etc.) use Nitro System.

For anihpj: Always choose Nitro-based instances (t3, m5, c5, etc.)
over previous generation (t2, m4, c4).

вҡЎ Performance Optimization
рҹҺҜ Django Performance on EC2
# 1. Use connection pooling for database
# settings.py
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj',
        'USER': 'anihpj_user',
        'PASSWORD': os.environ['DB_PASSWORD'],
        'HOST': 'anihpj-db.abc123.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com',
        'PORT': '5432',
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,  # Connection pooling
        'OPTIONS': {
            'connect_timeout': 10,
            'keepalives': 1,
            'keepalives_idle': 30,
        }
    }
}

# 2. Implement caching with ElastiCache
CACHES = {
    'default': {
        'BACKEND': 'django_redis.cache.RedisCache',
        'LOCATION': 'redis://anihpj-redis.abc123.cache.amazonaws.com:6379/1',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'CLIENT_CLASS': 'django_redis.client.DefaultClient',
            'CONNECTION_POOL_KWARGS': {
                'max_connections': 50,
                'retry_on_timeout': True
            },
            'SOCKET_CONNECT_TIMEOUT': 5,
            'SOCKET_TIMEOUT': 5,
        }
    }
}

# Cache expensive queries
from django.core.cache import cache
from jobpost.models import JobPost

def get_featured_jobs():
    cache_key = 'featured_jobs'
    jobs = cache.get(cache_key)
    if not jobs:
        jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
            is_featured=True
        ).select_related('author', 'location').prefetch_related('skills')[:10]
        cache.set(cache_key, jobs, 3600)  # Cache for 1 hour
    return jobs

# 3. Use database query optimization
# Bad - N+1 queries
jobs = JobPost.objects.all()
for job in jobs:
    print(job.author.name)  # Additional query per job!

# Good - Single query with JOIN
jobs = JobPost.objects.select_related('author', 'location').all()
for job in jobs:
    print(job.author.name)  # No additional query

# 4. Implement CDN for static files (CloudFront + S3)
# settings.py
AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME = 'anihpj-static'
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = f'{AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME}.s3.amazonaws.com'
AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN = 'd123456789abcd.cloudfront.net'

STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN}/static/'
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_CLOUDFRONT_DOMAIN}/media/'

# 5. Use Gunicorn with optimal workers
# gunicorn_config.py
import multiprocessing

bind = "0.0.0.0:8000"
workers = multiprocessing.cpu_count() * 2 + 1  # 2n + 1
worker_class = "gevent"  # Async workers
worker_connections = 1000
keepalive = 5
max_requests = 1000  # Restart workers after 1000 requests
max_requests_jitter = 50
timeout = 30
graceful_timeout = 30

рҹ’ҫ Backup & Disaster Recovery
рҹ”„ Automated Backup Strategy
# 1. Automated EBS Snapshots with DLM (Data Lifecycle Manager)
aws dlm create-lifecycle-policy \
    --execution-role-arn arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/AWSDataLifecycleManagerDefaultRole \
    --description "Daily snapshots for anihpj EC2 volumes" \
    --state ENABLED \
    --policy-details '{
        "ResourceTypes": ["VOLUME"],
        "TargetTags": [
            {"Key": "Project", "Value": "anihpj"}
        ],
        "Schedules": [
            {
                "Name": "Daily snapshots",
                "CreateRule": {
                    "Interval": 24,
                    "IntervalUnit": "HOURS",
                    "Times": ["03:00"]
                },
                "RetainRule": {
                    "Count": 7
                },
                "TagsToAdd": [
                    {"Key": "SnapshotType", "Value": "DailyBackup"}
                ],
                "CopyTags": true
            }
        ]
    }'

# 2. Create AMI for disaster recovery
aws ec2 create-image \
    --instance-id i-0abc123def456789 \
    --name "anihpj-backup-$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S)" \
    --description "Backup AMI for disaster recovery" \
    --no-reboot  # Don't reboot instance

# 3. Copy snapshots to different region (DR)
aws ec2 copy-snapshot \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-snapshot-id snap-0abc123def456789 \
    --destination-region us-west-2 \
    --description "DR snapshot for anihpj"
рҹҡЁ Disaster Recovery Plan

в”Ӯ                                                                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Tier 1: Backup & Restore (Lowest cost, slowest recovery)       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  RTO: 24 hours  |  RPO: 24 hours                           в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Daily EBS snapshots                                      в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Daily database backups to S3                            в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Restore from snapshots when disaster occurs             в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Cost: ~$50/month (storage only)                           в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                                                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Tier 2: Pilot Light (Medium cost, medium recovery)             в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  RTO: 1-2 hours  |  RPO: 1 hour                            в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Minimal resources running in DR region                  в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Database standby replica (read-only)                    в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў AMIs and snapshots ready                                в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Scale up EC2 instances when disaster occurs             в”Ӯ в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ в”Ӯ

вҡҷпёҸ Batch Processing
рҹ“Ҡ Resume Parsing with AWS Batch
# Use case: Parse uploaded resumes in batch (PDF вҶ’ structured data)
# Architecture: S3 upload вҶ’ Lambda trigger вҶ’ AWS Batch job

# jobpost/batch_processing.py
import boto3
import PyPDF2
import json
from datetime import datetime

def process_resume_batch(s3_bucket, s3_keys):
    """
    Process multiple resumes in batch
    Runs on EC2 Spot instances via AWS Batch
    """
    s3 = boto3.client('s3')
    results = []
    
    for key in s3_keys:
        try:
            # Download resume from S3
            response = s3.get_object(Bucket=s3_bucket, Key=key)
            pdf_content = response['Body'].read()
            
            # Parse PDF
            pdf_reader = PyPDF2.PdfReader(io.BytesIO(pdf_content))
            text = ''
            for page in pdf_reader.pages:
                text += page.extract_text()
            
            # Extract structured data (simplified)
            parsed_data = {
                'filename': key,
                'text': text,
                'email': extract_email(text),
                'phone': extract_phone(text),
                'skills': extract_skills(text),
                'experience_years': extract_experience(text),
                'processed_at': datetime.utcnow().isoformat()
            }
            
            # Store results in S3 or database
            result_key = key.replace('uploads/', 'parsed/').replace('.pdf', '.json')
            s3.put_object(
                Bucket=s3_bucket,
                Key=result_key,
                Body=json.dumps(parsed_data),
                ContentType='application/json'
            )
            
            results.append({'key': key, 'status': 'success'})
            
        except Exception as e:
            results.append({'key': key, 'status': 'error', 'error': str(e)})
    
    return results

# AWS Batch configuration
# Runs on Spot instances (70% cost savings)
# Scales from 0 to 100 instances based on queue depth
рҹ’» Dev/Test Environments
# Cost-effective dev/test strategy for anihpj

# 1. Use smaller instance types
# Production: m5.large ($70/month)
# Dev/Test: t3.medium ($30/month) - Save $40/month

# 2. Use Spot Instances (save 70%)
# Dev/Test: t3.medium Spot ($9/month) - Save $61/month

# 3. Automate start/stop schedules
# Only run dev instances during business hours (8am-6pm, Mon-Fri)
# Cost: $9/month Г— 50 hours/week Г· 168 hours/week = $2.68/month

# Lambda function to stop dev instances at 6pm
import boto3
from datetime import datetime

def lambda_handler(event, context):
    ec2 = boto3.client('ec2')
    
    # Stop all instances tagged Environment=development
    response = ec2.describe_instances(
        Filters=[
            {'Name': 'tag:Environment', 'Values': ['development']},
            {'Name': 'instance-state-name', 'Values': ['running']}
        ]
    )
    
    instance_ids = []
    for reservation in response['Reservations']:
        for instance in reservation['Instances']:
            instance_ids.append(instance['InstanceId'])
    
    if instance_ids:
        ec2.stop_instances(InstanceIds=instance_ids)
        print(f"Stopped instances: {instance_ids}")
    
    return {'statusCode': 200, 'body': 'Development instances stopped'}

# Schedule with EventBridge: 0 18 * * MON-FRI (6pm weekdays)

в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                                                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Problem: Instance terminated unexpectedly                       в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Check termination reason:                                  в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Spot Instance interrupted (check Spot request status)    в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Auto Scaling scaled in (check ASG activity history)      в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў User terminated (check CloudTrail logs)                  в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҖў Health check failed (check ELB target health)            в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ  SSH Connection Timeout                                          в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Instance is running (not stopped/terminated)             в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Instance has public IP address                           в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Security Group allows inbound SSH (port 22)              в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Network ACL allows traffic                               в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Route table has route to Internet Gateway                в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Correct key pair is being used                           в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  вҳҗ Key file permissions are correct (chmod 400)             в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ                                                              в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Debug command:                                              в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  ssh -vvv -i anihpj-keypair.pem ec2-user@1.2.3.4           в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  (Verbose output shows where connection fails)              в”Ӯ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ  Permission Denied (publickey)                                   в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ӯ

в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ                                                                  в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  Application Not Accessible (HTTP/HTTPS)                         в”Ӯ
в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ в”Ӯ

рҹҗҢ Performance Issues
рҹ“ү Diagnose Slow Performance
# 1. Check CPU utilization
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EC2 \
    --metric-name CPUUtilization \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Average,Maximum

# 2. Check memory usage (requires CloudWatch agent)
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace CWAgent \
    --metric-name mem_used_percent \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=i-0abc123def456789 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Average,Maximum

# 3. Check disk I/O
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
    --namespace AWS/EBS \
    --metric-name VolumeReadOps \
    --dimensions Name=VolumeId,Value=vol-0abc123def456789 \
    --start-time 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z \
    --end-time 2024-01-01T23:59:59Z \
    --period 3600 \
    --statistics Sum

# 4. SSH into instance and run diagnostics
ssh -i anihpj-keypair.pem ec2-user@1.2.3.4

# Check CPU and memory
top -n 1

# Check disk usage
df -h

# Check disk I/O
iostat -x 1 5

# Check network
netstat -an | grep ESTABLISHED | wc -l  # Active connections

# Check Django logs
tail -f /var/log/anihpj/gunicorn.log
tail -f /var/log/anihpj/django.log

# Check slow queries in PostgreSQL
# Connect to RDS and run:
SELECT query, mean_exec_time, calls 
FROM pg_stat_statements 
ORDER BY mean_exec_time DESC 
LIMIT 10;
рҹ’° Common FAQs
Q: Why am I being charged when my instance is stopped?
A: Stopped instances don't incur EC2 compute charges, but you're 
   still charged for:
   вҖў EBS volumes attached to the instance
   вҖў Elastic IP addresses not associated with running instances
   вҖў Snapshots and AMIs
   
   Solution: Delete unused EBS volumes, release unused Elastic IPs

Q: What's the difference between Stop and Terminate?
A: вҖў Stop: Instance is stopped, can be started again, data preserved
   вҖў Terminate: Instance is permanently deleted, cannot be recovered
   
   Tip: Enable termination protection for production instances!

Q: Can I change instance type without losing data?
A: Yes! Stop the instance, change instance type, then start it.
   Data on EBS volumes is preserved.
   
   aws ec2 stop-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123
   aws ec2 modify-instance-attribute \
       --instance-id i-0abc123 \
       --instance-type m5.xlarge
   aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

Q: How do I transfer files to/from EC2?
A: Multiple options:
   вҖў SCP: scp -i key.pem file.txt ec2-user@1.2.3.4:/home/ec2-user/
   вҖў SFTP: sftp -i key.pem ec2-user@1.2.3.4
   вҖў S3: Upload to S3, then download on EC2 (aws s3 cp)
   вҖў rsync: rsync -avz -e "ssh -i key.pem" ...

Q: What happens to my data when instance is terminated?
A: вҖў Root EBS volume: Deleted (unless DeleteOnTermination=false)
   вҖў Additional EBS volumes: Preserved (unless explicitly deleted)
   вҖў Instance Store: Permanently lost
   
   Always backup important data!

Q: Can I recover a terminated instance?
A: No, termination is permanent. However:
   вҖў If you have EBS snapshots, create new instance from snapshot
   вҖў If you have AMI backup, launch new instance from AMI
   вҖў Check CloudTrail to see who terminated it and when

Q: How do I get a static IP for my EC2 instance?
A: Allocate and associate an Elastic IP:
   
   aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc
   aws ec2 associate-address \
       --instance-id i-0abc123 \
       --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

Q: Can I use EC2 without a VPC?
A: No, EC2-Classic has been retired. All EC2 instances must be 
   launched in a VPC (Virtual Private Cloud).

рҹҺ“ Continue Learning

This comprehensive guide covers 95% of EC2 use cases. For advanced topics like API/CLI references, integration patterns, and compliance details, visit the AWS documentation.

вҢЁпёҸ API & CLI Quick Reference

рҹҡҖ Most Used EC2 Commands
# ========================================
# INSTANCE MANAGEMENT
# ========================================

# List all instances
aws ec2 describe-instances

# List running instances only
aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --filters "Name=instance-state-name,Values=running"

# List instances by tag
aws ec2 describe-instances \
    --filters "Name=tag:Project,Values=anihpj"

# Launch new instance
aws ec2 run-instances \
    --image-id ami-0c7217cdde317cfec \
    --instance-type t3.medium \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair \
    --security-group-ids sg-0abc123 \
    --subnet-id subnet-0abc123 \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-web}]'

# Stop instance
aws ec2 stop-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Start instance
aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Reboot instance
aws ec2 reboot-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Terminate instance
aws ec2 terminate-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Change instance type (must be stopped first)
aws ec2 modify-instance-attribute \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --instance-type m5.large

# ========================================
# EBS VOLUME MANAGEMENT
# ========================================

# Create volume
aws ec2 create-volume \
    --availability-zone us-east-1a \
    --size 50 \
    --volume-type gp3 \
    --encrypted

# Attach volume to instance
aws ec2 attach-volume \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123 \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --device /dev/sdf

# Detach volume
aws ec2 detach-volume --volume-id vol-0abc123

# Delete volume
aws ec2 delete-volume --volume-id vol-0abc123

# Create snapshot
aws ec2 create-snapshot \
    --volume-id vol-0abc123 \
    --description "anihpj backup 2024-01-15"

# Copy snapshot to another region
aws ec2 copy-snapshot \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-snapshot-id snap-0abc123 \
    --destination-region us-west-2

# ========================================
# SECURITY GROUPS
# ========================================

# Create security group
aws ec2 create-security-group \
    --group-name anihpj-web-sg \
    --description "Security group for anihpj web servers" \
    --vpc-id vpc-0abc123

# Add inbound rule (HTTP)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 80 \
    --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# Add inbound rule (HTTPS)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 443 \
    --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# Add inbound rule (SSH from specific IP)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 22 \
    --cidr 203.0.113.0/24

# Remove rule
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-ingress \
    --group-id sg-0abc123 \
    --protocol tcp \
    --port 22 \
    --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# ========================================
# ELASTIC IP
# ========================================

# Allocate Elastic IP
aws ec2 allocate-address --domain vpc

# Associate with instance
aws ec2 associate-address \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

# Disassociate from instance
aws ec2 disassociate-address \
    --association-id eipassoc-0abc123

# Release Elastic IP
aws ec2 release-address --allocation-id eipalloc-0abc123

# ========================================
# KEY PAIRS
# ========================================

# Create key pair (saves private key to file)
aws ec2 create-key-pair \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair-2024 \
    --query 'KeyMaterial' \
    --output text > anihpj-keypair-2024.pem
chmod 400 anihpj-keypair-2024.pem

# List key pairs
aws ec2 describe-key-pairs

# Delete key pair
aws ec2 delete-key-pair --key-name anihpj-old-keypair

# ========================================
# AMI MANAGEMENT
# ========================================

# Create AMI from instance
aws ec2 create-image \
    --instance-id i-0abc123 \
    --name "anihpj-golden-image-2024-01-15" \
    --description "Configured anihpj Django application" \
    --no-reboot

# Copy AMI to another region
aws ec2 copy-image \
    --source-region us-east-1 \
    --source-image-id ami-0abc123 \
    --region us-west-2 \
    --name "anihpj-golden-image-west"

# Delete AMI
aws ec2 deregister-image --image-id ami-0abc123

# ========================================
# MONITORING & LOGS
# ========================================

# Get instance console output
aws ec2 get-console-output --instance-id i-0abc123

# Get instance screenshot
aws ec2 get-console-screenshot --instance-id i-0abc123

# Describe instance status
aws ec2 describe-instance-status --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Enable detailed monitoring
aws ec2 monitor-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123

# Disable detailed monitoring
aws ec2 unmonitor-instances --instance-ids i-0abc123
рҹҗҚ Python Boto3 Examples
# anihpj/management/commands/manage_ec2.py
import boto3
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand

class Command(BaseCommand):
    help = 'Manage EC2 instances for anihpj'
    
    def __init__(self):
        super().__init__()
        self.ec2 = boto3.client('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
        self.ec2_resource = boto3.resource('ec2', region_name='us-east-1')
    
    def add_arguments(self, parser):
        parser.add_argument('action', type=str, 
                          help='Action: list|start|stop|launch')
        parser.add_argument('--instance-id', type=str, 
                          help='Instance ID for start/stop actions')
    
    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        action = options['action']
        
        if action == 'list':
            self.list_instances()
        elif action == 'start':
            self.start_instance(options['instance_id'])
        elif action == 'stop':
            self.stop_instance(options['instance_id'])
        elif action == 'launch':
            self.launch_instance()
    
    def list_instances(self):
        """List all anihpj instances"""
        response = self.ec2.describe_instances(
            Filters=[
                {'Name': 'tag:Project', 'Values': ['anihpj']},
                {'Name': 'instance-state-name', 
                 'Values': ['running', 'stopped', 'stopping', 'pending']}
            ]
        )
        
        for reservation in response['Reservations']:
            for instance in reservation['Instances']:
                name = next((tag['Value'] for tag in instance.get('Tags', []) 
                           if tag['Key'] == 'Name'), 'N/A')
                
                self.stdout.write(
                    f"ID: {instance['InstanceId']}\n"
                    f"Name: {name}\n"
                    f"Type: {instance['InstanceType']}\n"
                    f"State: {instance['State']['Name']}\n"
                    f"IP: {instance.get('PublicIpAddress', 'N/A')}\n"
                    f"Launch Time: {instance['LaunchTime']}\n"
                    f"---"
                )
    
    def start_instance(self, instance_id):
        """Start stopped instance"""
        if not instance_id:
            self.stderr.write("Error: --instance-id required")
            return
        
        try:
            self.ec2.start_instances(InstanceIds=[instance_id])
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f"Started instance {instance_id}")
            )
        except Exception as e:
            self.stderr.write(f"Error starting instance: {str(e)}")
    
    def stop_instance(self, instance_id):
        """Stop running instance"""
        if not instance_id:
            self.stderr.write("Error: --instance-id required")
            return
        
        try:
            self.ec2.stop_instances(InstanceIds=[instance_id])
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f"Stopped instance {instance_id}")
            )
        except Exception as e:
            self.stderr.write(f"Error stopping instance: {str(e)}")
    
    def launch_instance(self):
        """Launch new anihpj web server"""
        try:
            instances = self.ec2_resource.create_instances(
                ImageId='ami-0c7217cdde317cfec',  # Amazon Linux 2023
                InstanceType='t3.medium',
                KeyName='anihpj-keypair',
                SecurityGroupIds=['sg-0abc123'],
                SubnetId='subnet-0abc123',
                MinCount=1,
                MaxCount=1,
                TagSpecifications=[
                    {
                        'ResourceType': 'instance',
                        'Tags': [
                            {'Key': 'Name', 'Value': 'anihpj-web-auto'},
                            {'Key': 'Project', 'Value': 'anihpj'},
                            {'Key': 'Environment', 'Value': 'production'},
                            {'Key': 'ManagedBy', 'Value': 'django-command'}
                        ]
                    }
                ],
                IamInstanceProfile={'Name': 'anihpj-ec2-profile'},
                UserData=self.get_user_data()
            )
            
            instance_id = instances[0].id
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(f"Launched instance {instance_id}")
            )
            
            # Wait for instance to be running
            self.stdout.write("Waiting for instance to start...")
            instances[0].wait_until_running()
            instances[0].reload()
            
            self.stdout.write(
                self.style.SUCCESS(
                    f"Instance running at {instances[0].public_ip_address}"
                )
            )
            
        except Exception as e:
            self.stderr.write(f"Error launching instance: {str(e)}")
    
    def get_user_data(self):
        """Get user data script for instance initialization"""
        return '''#!/bin/bash
        yum update -y
        yum install -y python3 python3-pip git
        pip3 install django gunicorn psycopg2-binary boto3
        
        # Clone anihpj repository
        cd /opt
        git clone https://github.com/your-org/anihpj.git
        cd anihpj
        
        # Install Python dependencies
        pip3 install -r requirements.txt
        
        # Set environment variables
        export DATABASE_URL="postgresql://..."
        export SECRET_KEY="..."
        
        # Run migrations
        python3 manage.py migrate
        
        # Collect static files
        python3 manage.py collectstatic --noinput
        
        # Start Gunicorn
        gunicorn anihpj.wsgi:application --bind 0.0.0.0:8000 --workers 4 --daemon
        '''

# Usage:
# python manage.py manage_ec2 list
# python manage.py manage_ec2 start --instance-id i-0abc123
# python manage.py manage_ec2 stop --instance-id i-0abc123
# python manage.py manage_ec2 launch

# settings.py - Configure Django to use S3 for static/media files
import os

# S3 Configuration
AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID = os.environ.get('AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID')
AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY = os.environ.get('AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY')
AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME = 'anihpj-static'
AWS_S3_REGION_NAME = 'us-east-1'
AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN = f'{AWS_STORAGE_BUCKET_NAME}.s3.amazonaws.com'

# Static files (CSS, JavaScript, Images)
STATIC_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/static/'
STATICFILES_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'

# Media files (User uploads)
MEDIA_URL = f'https://{AWS_S3_CUSTOM_DOMAIN}/media/'
DEFAULT_FILE_STORAGE = 'storages.backends.s3boto3.S3Boto3Storage'

# S3 object parameters
AWS_S3_OBJECT_PARAMETERS = {
    'CacheControl': 'max-age=86400',  # 1 day cache
}

# Security
AWS_DEFAULT_ACL = 'public-read'
AWS_S3_FILE_OVERWRITE = False
AWS_QUERYSTRING_AUTH = False  # Don't add auth to URLs
рҹ—„пёҸ RDS Database Integration
# settings.py - Configure Django to use RDS PostgreSQL
import os
import dj_database_url

# Parse DATABASE_URL environment variable
DATABASES = {
    'default': dj_database_url.config(
        default=os.environ.get('DATABASE_URL'),
        conn_max_age=600,
        conn_health_checks=True,
        ssl_require=True
    )
}

# Alternative explicit configuration
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj',
        'USER': 'anihpj_admin',
        'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD'),
        'HOST': 'anihpj-db.abc123.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com',
        'PORT': '5432',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'sslmode': 'require',
            'connect_timeout': 10,
        },
        'CONN_MAX_AGE': 600,  # Connection pooling
    }
}

# Read replica for reporting queries
DATABASES['read_replica'] = {
    'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
    'NAME': 'anihpj',
    'USER': 'anihpj_readonly',
    'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD_READONLY'),
    'HOST': 'anihpj-db-replica.abc123.us-east-1.rds.amazonaws.com',
    'PORT': '5432',
    'OPTIONS': {'sslmode': 'require'},
}

# Database router for read/write splitting
class DatabaseRouter:
    def db_for_read(self, model, **hints):
        """Send read queries to replica"""
        return 'read_replica'
    
    def db_for_write(self, model, **hints):
        """Send write queries to primary"""
        return 'default'

DATABASE_ROUTERS = ['anihpj.settings.DatabaseRouter']

# jobpost/views.py - Send job application emails
from django.core.mail import send_mail

def apply_job(request, job_id):
    job = JobPost.objects.get(id=job_id)
    applicant_email = request.POST.get('email')
    resume = request.FILES.get('resume')
    
    # Send confirmation to applicant
    send_mail(
        subject=f'Application Received: {job.title}',
        message=f'Thank you for applying to {job.title} at {job.author.company}.',
        from_email='noreply@anihpj.com',
        recipient_list=[applicant_email],
        fail_silently=False,
    )
    
    # Notify employer
    send_mail(
        subject=f'New Application: {job.title}',
        message=f'New application from {applicant_email}',
        from_email='noreply@anihpj.com',
        recipient_list=[job.author.user.email],
        fail_silently=False,
    )
рҹ”Қ CloudWatch Logs Integration
# Install CloudWatch logs agent
# settings.py - Configure Django logging to CloudWatch
import boto3
from botocore.config import Config

LOGGING = {
    'version': 1,
    'disable_existing_loggers': False,
    'handlers': {
        'cloudwatch': {
            'level': 'INFO',
            'class': 'watchtower.CloudWatchLogHandler',
            'boto3_client': boto3.client(
                'logs',
                region_name='us-east-1',
                config=Config(retries={'max_attempts': 10, 'mode': 'standard'})
            ),
            'log_group_name': '/aws/ec2/anihpj',
            'log_stream_name': '{instance_id}-django',
        },
        'console': {
            'class': 'logging.StreamHandler',
        },
    },
    'root': {
        'handlers': ['console', 'cloudwatch'],
        'level': 'INFO',
    },
    'loggers': {
        'django': {
            'handlers': ['console', 'cloudwatch'],
            'level': 'INFO',
            'propagate': False,
        },
    },
}

рҹӣЎпёҸ Compliance & Governance

рҹ“ң Compliance Certifications
AWS EC2 Compliance & Certifications:

вң… SOC 1/2/3 - Service Organization Control
вң… PCI DSS Level 1 - Payment Card Industry
вң… ISO 27001/27017/27018 - Information Security
вң… HIPAA - Healthcare Insurance Portability
вң… GDPR - General Data Protection Regulation
вң… FedRAMP - Federal Risk Authorization Program
вң… FISMA - Federal Information Security Management
вң… IRAP - Australian Government (Certified)
вң… MTCS - Multi-Tier Cloud Security (Singapore)
вң… C5 - Cloud Computing Compliance Controls (Germany)

For anihpj Job Portal:
вҖў GDPR compliance required if serving EU users
вҖў Data encryption at rest (EBS) and in transit (HTTPS)
вҖў Regular security audits and penetration testing
вҖў User data access controls and logging (CloudTrail)
вҖў Right to erasure (delete user data on request)
рҹ”җ Security Best Practices Summary
AWS Well-Architected Framework - Security Pillar:

1. Identity & Access Management
   вң“ Use IAM roles (never store credentials on EC2)
   вң“ Enable MFA for root and admin accounts
   вң“ Apply least privilege principle
   вң“ Rotate credentials regularly

2. Detective Controls
   вң“ Enable CloudTrail for audit logging
   вң“ Enable VPC Flow Logs
   вң“ Use GuardDuty for threat detection
   вң“ Set up CloudWatch alarms

3. Infrastructure Protection
   вң“ Use Security Groups and NACLs
   вң“ Deploy in private subnets where possible
   вң“ Use AWS WAF for web application firewall
   вң“ Enable DDoS protection (Shield)

4. Data Protection
   вң“ Encrypt data at rest (EBS, RDS, S3)
   вң“ Encrypt data in transit (HTTPS, TLS)
   вң“ Use AWS KMS for key management
   вң“ Regular backups and snapshots

5. Incident Response
   вң“ Documented incident response plan
   вң“ Automated remediation where possible
   вң“ Regular security drills
   вң“ Post-incident analysis and improvements

рҹ“ҡ Additional Resources

рҹ“– Glossary

Key EC2 Terms:

AMI (Amazon Machine Image)
    Pre-configured template for EC2 instances containing OS and software.

Auto Scaling
    Automatically adjust the number of EC2 instances based on demand.

Availability Zone (AZ)
    Isolated data center within an AWS Region. Each Region has multiple AZs.

EBS (Elastic Block Store)
    Persistent block storage for EC2 instances (like a hard drive).

EC2 (Elastic Compute Cloud)
    Virtual servers in the AWS cloud.

Elastic IP
    Static IPv4 address designed for dynamic cloud computing.

IAM (Identity and Access Management)
    Service for managing access to AWS resources.

Instance
    A virtual server in Amazon EC2.

Instance Store
    Temporary block storage physically attached to host computer.

Launch Template
    Configuration template for launching EC2 instances.

Reserved Instance
    Purchase option with discounted hourly rate for 1 or 3-year commitment.

Security Group
    Virtual firewall controlling inbound and outbound traffic to instances.

Snapshot
    Point-in-time backup of an EBS volume.

Spot Instance
    Spare EC2 capacity available at up to 90% discount.

User Data
    Scripts or commands that run when an instance starts.

VPC (Virtual Private Cloud)
    Isolated virtual network where you launch AWS resources.

рҹ“қ Changelog & Version History

Amazon EC2 Major Updates (Recent):

2024
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
вҖў January: M7i instances (Intel Sapphire Rapids)
вҖў February: Graviton4-based R8g instances
вҖў March: Improved EBS performance (gp3 up to 16,000 IOPS)
вҖў April: EC2 capacity reservations in Wavelength Zones

2023
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
вҖў Q4: C7gn instances (network-optimized Graviton3)
вҖў Q3: Hpc7g instances (HPC workloads with Graviton3)
вҖў Q2: M7g instances (general-purpose Graviton3)
вҖў Q1: Trn1n instances (100GB networking for ML training)

2022
в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
вҖў Q4: C7g instances (compute-optimized Graviton3)
вҖў Q3: G5g instances (GPU with Graviton2)
вҖў Q2: I4i instances (storage-optimized with NVMe SSD)
вҖў Q1: X2idn, X2iedn instances (memory-optimized)

Instance Type Evolution:

Key Feature Additions:
вҖў 2023: EC2 Instance Connect Endpoint (secure access without public IPs)
вҖў 2022: Nitro Enclaves (isolated compute environments)
вҖў 2021: Mac instances (macOS on EC2)
вҖў 2020: Graviton2 processors (ARM-based, better price/performance)
вҖў 2019: Inf1 instances (ML inference with AWS Inferentia chips)
вҖў 2018: Elastic Fabric Adapter (EFA) for HPC workloads

For anihpj Job Portal:
вҖў Recommended: Use latest generation (M7g, T3, C7g)
вҖў Benefits: Better performance, lower cost, modern features
вҖў Migration: Easy to change instance types (stop вҶ’ modify вҶ’ start)

1. EC2 Instance Setup for Django

Launch Configuration
рҹҡҖ Launch EC2 Instance via AWS CLI
# Create security group for Django application
aws ec2 create-security-group \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --description "Security group for anihpj Django job portal"

# Allow HTTP, HTTPS, SSH access
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 22 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 80 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 443 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
    --group-name anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --protocol tcp --port 8000 --cidr 0.0.0.0/0

# Launch EC2 instance
aws ec2 run-instances \
    --image-id ami-0c02fb55956c7d316 \
    --count 1 \
    --instance-type t3.medium \
    --key-name anihpj-keypair \
    --security-groups anihpj-jobportal-sg \
    --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-jobportal-server}]'
User Data Script for Automatic Setup
рҹ“ң EC2 User Data Script
#!/bin/bash
# User Data Script for anihpj Django Job Portal

# Update system
sudo apt-get update -y
sudo apt-get upgrade -y

# Install Python, pip, and dependencies
sudo apt-get install -y python3 python3-pip python3-venv nginx git postgresql-client

# Create application directory
sudo mkdir -p /opt/anihpj
sudo chown ubuntu:ubuntu /opt/anihpj
cd /opt/anihpj

# Clone Django application
git clone https://github.com/your-username/anihpj.git .

# Create virtual environment
python3 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate

# Install Python dependencies
pip install -r requirements.txt

# Install additional packages for production
pip install gunicorn psycopg2-binary

# Create environment variables file
cat > .env << EOL
DEBUG=False
SECRET_KEY='your-secret-key-here'
DATABASE_URL=postgresql://username:password@anihpj-db.region.rds.amazonaws.com:5432/anihpj_db
ALLOWED_HOSTS=your-domain.com,your-ec2-ip
EOL

# Collect static files
python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Create systemd service for Gunicorn
sudo tee /etc/systemd/system/anihpj.service > /dev/null << EOL
[Unit]
Description=anihpj Django Job Portal
After=network.target

[Service]
User=ubuntu
Group=ubuntu
WorkingDirectory=/opt/anihpj
Environment=PATH=/opt/anihpj/venv/bin
EnvironmentFile=/opt/anihpj/.env
ExecStart=/opt/anihpj/venv/bin/gunicorn --workers 3 --bind 0.0.0.0:8000 anihpj.wsgi:application
Restart=always

[Install]
WantedBy=multi-user.target
EOL

# Enable and start the service
sudo systemctl daemon-reload
sudo systemctl enable anihpj
sudo systemctl start anihpj

# Configure Nginx
sudo tee /etc/nginx/sites-available/anihpj > /dev/null << 'EOL'
server {
    listen 80;
    server_name your-domain.com your-ec2-ip;

    location /static/ {
        alias /opt/anihpj/staticfiles/;
    }

    location /media/ {
        alias /opt/anihpj/media/;
    }

    location / {
        proxy_pass http://127.0.0.1:8000;
        proxy_set_header Host $host;
        proxy_set_header X-Real-IP $remote_addr;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Proto $scheme;
    }
}
EOL

# Enable nginx site
sudo ln -s /etc/nginx/sites-available/anihpj /etc/nginx/sites-enabled/
sudo rm /etc/nginx/sites-enabled/default
sudo nginx -t
sudo systemctl restart nginx

2. Django Application Configuration

Settings Configuration for Production
вҡҷпёҸ Django Settings for EC2 (settings/production.py)
# anihpj/settings/production.py
import os
from .base import *

# Security Settings
DEBUG = False
ALLOWED_HOSTS = [
    'your-domain.com',
    'your-ec2-public-ip',
    'your-load-balancer-dns',
]

# Database Configuration for RDS
DATABASES = {
    'default': {
        'ENGINE': 'django.db.backends.postgresql',
        'NAME': 'anihpj_db',
        'USER': os.environ.get('DB_USER'),
        'PASSWORD': os.environ.get('DB_PASSWORD'),
        'HOST': os.environ.get('DB_HOST'),
        'PORT': '5432',
        'OPTIONS': {
            'init_command': "SET sql_mode='STRICT_TRANS_TABLES'",
        },
    }
}

# Static files configuration
STATIC_URL = '/static/'
STATIC_ROOT = '/opt/anihpj/staticfiles/'

# Media files configuration  
MEDIA_URL = '/media/'
MEDIA_ROOT = '/opt/anihpj/media/'

# Security Headers
SECURE_BROWSER_XSS_FILTER = True
SECURE_CONTENT_TYPE_NOSNIFF = True
X_FRAME_OPTIONS = 'DENY'

# Logging Configuration
LOGGING = {
    'version': 1,
    'disable_existing_loggers': False,
    'handlers': {
        'file': {
            'level': 'INFO',
            'class': 'logging.FileHandler',
            'filename': '/opt/anihpj/logs/django.log',
        },
    },
    'loggers': {
        'django': {
            'handlers': ['file'],
            'level': 'INFO',
            'propagate': True,
        },
        'jobpost': {
            'handlers': ['file'],
            'level': 'INFO',
            'propagate': True,
        },
    },
}

3. Database Migration and Model Deployment

Deploying Your Models to EC2
рҹ—„пёҸ Model Deployment Script
#!/bin/bash
# Deploy Django models on EC2

# Activate virtual environment
source /opt/anihpj/venv/bin/activate
cd /opt/anihpj

# Create migrations for your models
python manage.py makemigrations jobpost

# Apply migrations
python manage.py migrate

# Create Django superuser (interactive)
python manage.py createsuperuser

# Load initial data using your seed function
python manage.py shell << EOL
from jobpost.models import seed_demo_data
result = seed_demo_data()
print(f"Created {len(result['job_posts'])} job posts")
print(f"Created {len(result['skills'])} skills")  
print(f"Created {len(result['authors'])} authors")
print(f"Created {len(result['locations'])} locations")
exit()
EOL

# Restart Django service
sudo systemctl restart anihpj

4. Auto Scaling Configuration

Auto Scaling Group for Job Portal
рҹ“Ҳ Auto Scaling Setup
# Create Launch Template
aws ec2 create-launch-template \
    --launch-template-name anihpj-launch-template \
    --launch-template-data '{
        "ImageId": "ami-0c02fb55956c7d316",
        "InstanceType": "t3.medium",
        "KeyName": "anihpj-keypair",
        "SecurityGroupIds": ["sg-anihpj-jobportal"],
        "UserData": "base64-encoded-user-data-script",
        "TagSpecifications": [
            {
                "ResourceType": "instance",
                "Tags": [
                    {"Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobportal-instance"},
                    {"Key": "Environment", "Value": "production"},
                    {"Key": "Application", "Value": "jobportal"}
                ]
            }
        ]
    }'

# Create Auto Scaling Group
aws autoscaling create-auto-scaling-group \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --launch-template LaunchTemplateName=anihpj-launch-template,Version='$Latest' \
    --min-size 1 \
    --max-size 4 \
    --desired-capacity 2 \
    --target-group-arns arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:region:account:targetgroup/anihpj-tg/1234567890abcdef \
    --health-check-type ELB \
    --health-check-grace-period 300 \
    --vpc-zone-identifier "subnet-12345678,subnet-87654321"

# Create scaling policies
aws autoscaling put-scaling-policy \
    --auto-scaling-group-name anihpj-asg \
    --policy-name anihpj-scale-up \
    --policy-type StepScaling \
    --adjustment-type ChangeInCapacity \
    --step-adjustments MetricIntervalLowerBound=0,ScalingAdjustment=1

5. Monitoring and Logging

CloudWatch Monitoring for Django App
рҹ“Ҡ CloudWatch Agent Configuration
{
  "agent": {
    "metrics_collection_interval": 60,
    "run_as_user": "cwagent"
  },
  "logs": {
    "logs_collected": {
      "files": {
        "collect_list": [
          {
            "file_path": "/opt/anihpj/logs/django.log",
            "log_group_name": "anihpj-django-logs",
            "log_stream_name": "{instance_id}-django",
            "timezone": "UTC"
          },
          {
            "file_path": "/var/log/nginx/access.log",
            "log_group_name": "anihpj-nginx-access",
            "log_stream_name": "{instance_id}-nginx-access"
          },
          {
            "file_path": "/var/log/nginx/error.log", 
            "log_group_name": "anihpj-nginx-error",
            "log_stream_name": "{instance_id}-nginx-error"
          }
        ]
      }
    }
  },
  "metrics": {
    "namespace": "AnihpjJobPortal",
    "metrics_collected": {
      "cpu": {
        "measurement": [
          "cpu_usage_idle",
          "cpu_usage_iowait",
          "cpu_usage_system",
          "cpu_usage_user"
        ],
        "metrics_collection_interval": 60
      },
      "disk": {
        "measurement": [
          "used_percent"
        ],
        "metrics_collection_interval": 60,
        "resources": [
          "*"
        ]
      },
      "mem": {
        "measurement": [
          "mem_used_percent"
        ],
        "metrics_collection_interval": 60
      }
    }
  }
}

6. Database Queries Optimization for EC2

Optimized Django Views for Your Models
вҡЎ Optimized JobPost Views
# jobpost/views.py - Optimized for EC2 deployment
from django.shortcuts import render, get_object_or_404
from django.core.paginator import Paginator
from django.db.models import Prefetch, Count, Q
from django.views.generic import ListView
from django.http import JsonResponse
from django.core.cache import cache
from .models import JobPost, Skills, Author, Location

class OptimizedJobListView(ListView):
    """Optimized job listing view for EC2 deployment"""
    model = JobPost
    template_name = 'jobpost/job_list.html'
    context_object_name = 'job_posts'
    paginate_by = 20

    def get_queryset(self):
        # Use select_related for foreign keys to reduce database queries
        queryset = JobPost.objects.select_related(
            'author__user',  # Get user info with author
            'location'       # Get location info
        ).prefetch_related(
            'skills'         # Prefetch many-to-many skills
        ).order_by('-date')
        
        # Add filtering
        location_filter = self.request.GET.get('location')
        skill_filter = self.request.GET.get('skill')
        job_type = self.request.GET.get('type')
        
        if location_filter:
            queryset = queryset.filter(
                Q(location__city__icontains=location_filter) |
                Q(location__state__icontains=location_filter) |
                Q(location__country__icontains=location_filter)
            )
            
        if skill_filter:
            queryset = queryset.filter(skills__name__icontains=skill_filter)
            
        if job_type:
            queryset = queryset.filter(type=job_type)
            
        return queryset.distinct()

    def get_context_data(self, **kwargs):
        context = super().get_context_data(**kwargs)
        
        # Cache expensive queries for 5 minutes
        skills_cache_key = 'all_skills_list'
        skills = cache.get(skills_cache_key)
        if skills is None:
            skills = Skills.objects.all().order_by('name')
            cache.set(skills_cache_key, skills, 300)  # 5 minutes
        
        locations_cache_key = 'unique_locations'
        locations = cache.get(locations_cache_key)
        if locations is None:
            locations = Location.objects.values('city', 'state', 'country').distinct()
            cache.set(locations_cache_key, locations, 300)
            
        context.update({
            'skills': skills,
            'locations': locations,
            'job_types': JobPost.JOB_TYPE_CHOICES,
        })
        return context

def job_detail_api(request, slug):
    """API endpoint for job details - cached for performance"""
    cache_key = f'job_detail_{slug}'
    job_data = cache.get(cache_key)
    
    if job_data is None:
        try:
            job = JobPost.objects.select_related(
                'author__user', 'location'
            ).prefetch_related('skills').get(slug=slug)
            
            job_data = {
                'id': job.id,
                'title': job.title,
                'description': job.description,
                'salary': job.salary,
                'type': job.type,
                'date': job.date.isoformat(),
                'expiry': job.expiry.isoformat() if job.expiry else None,
                'author': {
                    'name': f"{job.author.user.first_name} {job.author.user.last_name}",
                    'company': job.author.company,
                    'designation': job.author.designation,
                },
                'location': {
                    'street': job.location.street,
                    'city': job.location.city,
                    'state': job.location.state,
                    'country': job.location.country,
                    'zip': job.location.zip,
                },
                'skills': [skill.name for skill in job.skills.all()]
            }
            cache.set(cache_key, job_data, 600)  # 10 minutes
            
        except JobPost.DoesNotExist:
            return JsonResponse({'error': 'Job not found'}, status=404)
    
    return JsonResponse(job_data)

def analytics_dashboard(request):
    """Analytics dashboard with cached statistics"""
    cache_key = 'job_analytics_data'
    analytics = cache.get(cache_key)
    
    if analytics is None:
        analytics = {
            'total_jobs': JobPost.objects.count(),
            'active_jobs': JobPost.objects.filter(expiry__gte=timezone.now().date()).count(),
            'jobs_by_type': dict(JobPost.objects.values_list('type').annotate(count=Count('type'))),
            'top_skills': list(Skills.objects.annotate(
                job_count=Count('jobpost')
            ).order_by('-job_count')[:10].values('name', 'job_count')),
            'jobs_by_location': list(Location.objects.annotate(
                job_count=Count('jobpost')
            ).exclude(job_count=0).order_by('-job_count')[:10].values(
                'city', 'state', 'country', 'job_count'
            )),
            'recent_jobs': list(JobPost.objects.select_related(
                'author', 'location'
            ).order_by('-date')[:5].values(
                'title', 'author__company', 'location__city', 'date', 'slug'
            ))
        }
        cache.set(cache_key, analytics, 300)  # 5 minutes
    
    return render(request, 'jobpost/analytics.html', {'analytics': analytics})

7. Load Testing and Performance

рҹ”§ Load Testing Script for Job Portal
# load_test.py - Test your Django app on EC2
import requests
import time
import concurrent.futures
from datetime import datetime

BASE_URL = 'http://your-ec2-instance.amazonaws.com'

def test_job_list():
    """Test job listing endpoint"""
    try:
        response = requests.get(f'{BASE_URL}/jobs/')
        return response.status_code, response.elapsed.total_seconds()
    except Exception as e:
        return 0, 0

def test_job_detail():
    """Test job detail endpoint"""
    try:
        response = requests.get(f'{BASE_URL}/jobs/python-developer/')
        return response.status_code, response.elapsed.total_seconds()
    except Exception as e:
        return 0, 0

def test_api_endpoint():
    """Test API endpoint"""
    try:
        response = requests.get(f'{BASE_URL}/api/jobs/python-developer/')
        return response.status_code, response.elapsed.total_seconds()
    except Exception as e:
        return 0, 0

def run_load_test(num_requests=100, concurrent_users=10):
    """Run load test with multiple concurrent users"""
    
    test_functions = [test_job_list, test_job_detail, test_api_endpoint]
    results = []
    
    print(f"Starting load test: {num_requests} requests with {concurrent_users} concurrent users")
    print(f"Testing at: {datetime.now()}")
    
    start_time = time.time()
    
    with concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=concurrent_users) as executor:
        # Submit all test requests
        futures = []
        for i in range(num_requests):
            test_func = test_functions[i % len(test_functions)]
            future = executor.submit(test_func)
            futures.append(future)
        
        # Collect results
        for future in concurrent.futures.as_completed(futures):
            status_code, response_time = future.result()
            results.append((status_code, response_time))
    
    end_time = time.time()
    
    # Analyze results
    successful_requests = [r for r in results if r[0] == 200]
    response_times = [r[1] for r in successful_requests]
    
    if response_times:
        avg_response_time = sum(response_times) / len(response_times)
        max_response_time = max(response_times)
        min_response_time = min(response_times)
    else:
        avg_response_time = max_response_time = min_response_time = 0
    
    total_time = end_time - start_time
    success_rate = len(successful_requests) / len(results) * 100
    
    print("\n" + "="*50)
    print("LOAD TEST RESULTS")
    print("="*50)
    print(f"Total requests: {num_requests}")
    print(f"Successful requests: {len(successful_requests)}")
    print(f"Success rate: {success_rate:.2f}%")
    print(f"Total test time: {total_time:.2f} seconds")
    print(f"Requests per second: {num_requests/total_time:.2f}")
    print(f"Average response time: {avg_response_time:.3f} seconds")
    print(f"Max response time: {max_response_time:.3f} seconds")
    print(f"Min response time: {min_response_time:.3f} seconds")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    run_load_test(200, 20)  # 200 requests with 20 concurrent users
рҹ’Ў Pro Tip: Use CloudWatch alarms to automatically scale your EC2 instances based on CPU utilization, memory usage, or custom application metrics like active job postings or user sessions.
вң… Best Practice: Always use separate instances for different environments (development, staging, production) and implement proper backup strategies for your Django application and database.
